  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_2c828a02-d71d-4c4d-8b20-78553186f647'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

<span id="freeTextContainer9821193125644564328">The Caleighs have had a terrible year...They need time and space, while they await the news they dread. Gabe has brought his wife, Eve, and daughters, Loren and Cally, down to Devon, to the peaceful seaside village of Hollow Bay. He can work and Eve and the kids can have some peace and quiet and perhaps they can try, as a family, to come to terms with what's happened to th</span>
  <span id="freeText9821193125644564328" style="display:none">The Caleighs have had a terrible year...They need time and space, while they await the news they dread. Gabe has brought his wife, Eve, and daughters, Loren and Cally, down to Devon, to the peaceful seaside village of Hollow Bay. He can work and Eve and the kids can have some peace and quiet and perhaps they can try, as a family, to come to terms with what's happened to them...Crickley Hall is an unusually large house on the outskirts of the village at the bottom of Devil's Cleave, a massive tree-lined gorge - the stuff of local legend. A river flows past the front garden. It's perfect for them...if it a bit gloomy. And Chester, their dog, seems really spooked at being away from home. And old houses do make sounds. And it's constantly cold. And even though they shut the cellar door every night, it's always open again in morning The Secret of Crickley Hall is James Herbert's finest novel to date. It explores the darker, more obtuse territories of evil and the supernatural. With brooding menace and rising tension, he masterfully and relentlessly draws the reader through to the ultimate revelation one that will stay to chill the mind long after the book has been laid aside.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9821193125644564328" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_744401982" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/744401982" />
    <a title="Apatt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2457095-apatt"><img alt="Apatt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1349239948p2/2457095.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/744401982?book_show_action=true">Oct 18, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Apatt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Apatt" href="/user/show/2457095-apatt">Apatt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2457095-apatt?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer744401982" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10774915671215208833">It’s almost Halloween as I write so I’m in the mood for some creepy read. If you are ever in the mood for horror fiction and you have never read anything by James Herbert you have been outrageously remiss. In the 70s and 80s James Herbert was King, practically <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3389.Stephen_King' title='Stephen King' rel='nofollow noopener'>Stephen King</a> as teens and horror fans were reading his books all over the place (in the UK where I was residing any way I have no idea about Herbertism in other countries). His most widely known book <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/397867.The_Rats__Rats___1_' title='The Rats (Rats, #1) by James Herbert' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Rats</a> was published in 1974 it was a</span>
  <span id="freeText10774915671215208833" style="display:none">It’s almost Halloween as I write so I’m in the mood for some creepy read. If you are ever in the mood for horror fiction and you have never read anything by James Herbert you have been outrageously remiss. In the 70s and 80s James Herbert was King, practically <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3389.Stephen_King" title="Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener">Stephen King</a> as teens and horror fans were reading his books all over the place (in the UK where I was residing any way I have no idea about Herbertism in other countries). His most widely known book <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/397867.The_Rats__Rats___1_" title="The Rats (Rats, #1) by James Herbert" rel="nofollow noopener">The Rats</a> was published in 1974 it was a barnstorming debut, an ultra-violent, graphic and horrific little novel about mutant rats. His second novel <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/397860.The_Fog" title="The Fog by James Herbert" rel="nofollow noopener">The Fog</a> was even worse (or better, depends on how you look at it). He was 31 at the time.<br><i>The Secret Of Crickley Hall</i> was published in 2006 when Herbert was 63, I would say age has mellowed him over the years. That said, “Crickley” still pretty damn gruesome in places and not for the faint of heart. However, in addition to the Herbertian patented ew! factor this book is also quite compassionate, poignant and even sentimental. A lot of care and attention has been put into developing the characters.<br><br>This is basically a haunted house story, not a first from Mr. Herbert (see <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/397868.Haunted__David_Ash___1_" title="Haunted (David Ash, #1) by James Herbert" rel="nofollow noopener">Haunted</a>. All the haunted house tropes are in place; a nice family (with cute kids and a dog) move into a spooky old house with a dark history, things soon start to go bump in the night. The wife is open to the idea of supernatural phenomena, but the husband is extremely skeptical, soon a psychic and even a paranormal investigator show up. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1571883160i/28342040.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>From the BBC adaptation<br><br>The book is saved from becoming pointlessly predictable by the characterization, the gradually unfolding backstory of the eponymous house and Herbert’s sheer storytelling skills. I haven't read anything by him for years; I have forgotten how good he was at grabbing your attention and never letting go. However, the backstory of the house does involve some scenes of extreme cruelty to children so if you are easily offended by such scenes this book is seriously not for you. Even so, the theme of children’s basic right to love, comfort and protection is evident and even highlighted by the harrowing details of their ordeal. I don’t think the author’s intention is to titillate, not something that can be said about the violent scenes in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/397867.The_Rats__Rats___1_" title="The Rats (Rats, #1) by James Herbert" rel="nofollow noopener">The Rats</a>. If I have a complaint it would be the characterization of Gabe the skeptical husband whose extreme skepticism in the face of extremely weird occurrences make him seem like an imbecile of the first water. The way he relentlessly rationalizes the unrationalizable makes me want to improve his outlook with a frying pan.<br><br>The supernatural events in the story are vividly depicted and very creepy, as you would expect from an author who has been writing such material for decades. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1221698.Neil_Gaiman" title="Neil Gaiman" rel="nofollow noopener">Neil Gaiman</a> said this of James Herbert: <i>“His first book was a bestseller, which is something that happens to very few writers. He had to do all his growing up in public. He had to learn to write in public.”</i>. His growth as a writer over the decades of his career has been tremendous. His prose is highly readable, often witty without ever becoming clumsy; it makes for a very smooth reading experience. <br><br>Sadly James Herbert passed away a few months ago (March 2013), so this review is intended to be something of a tribute. Thanks to his prolificacy while I have read many books by him there are still many that I have yet to read. <br><br>R.I.P. Mr. Herbert, you were the best.<br><br><b>Note:</b> <i>The Secret Of Crickley Hall</i> was <a href="http://www.bbc.co.uk/programmes/p00t081w" rel="nofollow noopener">adapted by the BBC</a> and broadcasted in 2012. Not as good as the book but pretty good!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1571882886i/28342037.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="10774915671215208833" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review744401982">

<span id="freeTextContainer17759473224925163304"><br/><b> I'M UPSET! </b><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459256043i/18587688.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><i>*deep breaths*</i><br/><br/>One of the things that ticks me off – <b>IS FALSE ADVERTISING!</b><br/>I have been conned and I’m furious! Well to be precised, Ben and I have been conned and going by his status updates – as you witnessed, F bombs were practically on every progress updates, he wasn’t too impresses either.<br/><br/>Let’s analyze. <br/><br/>The synopsis said:<br/><i>The Secret of Crickley Hall is a new take on the classic <b><u>ghost story</u></b> in the same way that his bestseller Once was a new take on the classic fairy tale. The Secret </i></span>
  <span id="freeText17759473224925163304" style="display:none"><br><b> I'M UPSET! </b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459256043i/18587688.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>*deep breaths*</i><br><br>One of the things that ticks me off – <b>IS FALSE ADVERTISING!</b><br>I have been conned and I’m furious! Well to be precised, Ben and I have been conned and going by his status updates – as you witnessed, F bombs were practically on every progress updates, he wasn’t too impresses either.<br><br>Let’s analyze. <br><br>The synopsis said:<br><i>The Secret of Crickley Hall is a new take on the classic <b><u>ghost story</u></b> in the same way that his bestseller Once was a new take on the classic fairy tale. The Secret of Crickley Hall is set in a childrens home in a coastal town in England. Some of the children are persecuted by the people who run the home and have found places between the floors and walls of the home to avoid the adults. They can also spy, of course. One day there is a flash flood which sweeps through the town and the childrens home. All the children escape, except the kids in the walls and floors, who drown. <b><u>They come back as ghosts and seek their revenge.</u></b></i><br><br>Now that's out of the way, let’s focus on the underlined ones, shall we?<br><br>Point one.<br><i> Ghost Story.</i> When you read or hear this word, first thing that comes to mind is scary.<br>And scary by definition is ----&gt; causing fright or alarm; frightening; causing fear.<br>The synopsis mentioned ghost story, hence the expectations. So, did I quake in my boots then? FARKING NO! Not even a tiniest shake happened to me. You know what had scared me more? It was when I took my driving test many moons ago!<br>Look, there were ghosts in the story all right but they were nowhere scary. Very tame and others were just plain disgusting but <b>NOT SCARY.</b><br><br>Point two.<br><i>They come back as ghosts and seek their revenge</i><br>Ghosts + revenge = unimaginable pain (and horror), right? NOOOOOOOO! Not in this f*n story again! I was downright disappointed! <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459256043i/18587689.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Revenge (for me) should be fatal. Revenge should offer unparalleled pain.<br>Revenge should make the m*therf*r suffers six ways to Sundays. Otherwise, it's not revenge, you see.<br><br>So, what did we REALLY have here then?<br><br>1. Flagellation<br>2. Child abuse<br>3. Mutilation<br>4. Statutory rape<br>5. Killings<br>6. Cynicism <br>7. Clairvoyance<br><br>See? False advertising!<br>HA!<br><br>This should earn 0 star rating for me but you know what, I should also be honest and point it out here that the story was good. Not to mention the twist of the one character was unexpected. But sad to say, it was too late. IT WAS DAMN TOO LATE. And even though the story was pretty decent, it was painfully slow. <br>I dunno if I'd<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459256043i/18587690.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Or <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459256043i/18587691.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>on every single chapter I finished. But I endured the excruciatingly slow progress of this story and have turned the last page of it. <br>The choir I stashed in my head grabbed their trumpets and sang <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459256787i/18587841.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>Rating this <b>1</b> <i>It's-not-you-Ben-but-it's-the-false-advertisement</i> <b>Star</b><br><br>I enjoyed this BR, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/16968146-benjamin-stahl" rel="nofollow noopener">Ben</a> even though it didn't turn out that way we wanted it to be.<br>Till next time and yes it's my choosing.<br><b>*rubs hands mischievously*</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459256043i/18587692.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>___________________<br><br>OMG! I.<b>BLEEP</b>.FINALLY.FINISHED.THIS.<b>BLEEP!</b><br>I dunno if I'm gonna cry, dance or <u>HURL SOMETHING ACROSS THE ROOM.</u><br>Ooooooh <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/16968146-benjamin-stahl" rel="nofollow noopener">Ben</a> <b>*shakes head*</b><br>Ben. Ben. Ben.Ben. You will see how I loved this <s>mother</s> <b>BLEEP!</b><br><br>Review to come when my mental state is no longer questionable.<br><br><br>__________<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1456662896ra/18263906.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And the scaring commences tomorrow!<br>Bring it on!<br><br>_________<br>CAN'T WAIT TO QUAKE IN MY BOOTS.<br>My <b> FIRST </b> buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/16968146-benjamin-stahl" rel="nofollow noopener">Ben</a> <br>Starts on 15 March.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bill" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bill" href="/user/show/844726-bill">Bill</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/844726-bill?shelf=james-herbert">james-herbert</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer13835802" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4858439139316030373">I have read most if nota all of James Herbert's books and I think he has written some excellent novels (Fluke, Portent, '48) and some that I wasn't so keen on (notably The Spear)<br/><br/>However with The Secret Of Crickley Hall I think he has done a fantastic job. I would say this just edges Portent from my top 3 Herbert books<br/><br/>The characterisations are wonderful the plot is superb and the build up is one of his best.<br/><br/>I really used to enjoy reading Denis Wheatley books when I was younger, one thing I loved </span>
  <span id="freeText4858439139316030373" style="display:none">I have read most if nota all of James Herbert's books and I think he has written some excellent novels (Fluke, Portent, '48) and some that I wasn't so keen on (notably The Spear)<br /><br />However with The Secret Of Crickley Hall I think he has done a fantastic job. I would say this just edges Portent from my top 3 Herbert books<br /><br />The characterisations are wonderful the plot is superb and the build up is one of his best.<br /><br />I really used to enjoy reading Denis Wheatley books when I was younger, one thing I loved about Wheatley was that he always seemed to make me want to read just one more chapter, so at times I'd read for far longer than I'd perhaps planned. This book for me is very much like that<br /><br />Detractors may say that it's just a haunted house story, well maybe it is but it is superbly well written with some great plot twists<br /><br />If you're a James Herbert fan you've probably already read this, if you're not or you've never read any of his novels then I think this would be an excellent place to start</span>
  <a data-text-id="4858439139316030373" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer862671698" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13495792007903771300">The is THE HAUNTED HOUSE STORY YOU MUST READ.<br/>Easily my favourite book this year, The Secret of Crickley Hall is the quintessential haunted house story. So often we pick up haunted house books thinking it's going to be full of ghosts and poltergeists and stormy nights and scary settings, only to spend 300 pages waiting for the ghosts to appear that never do.<br/>This book is 600 pages of pure, unadulterated, haunted house goodness. There are good spirits, there are bad spirits, there is a big old mano</span>
  <span id="freeText13495792007903771300" style="display:none">The is THE HAUNTED HOUSE STORY YOU MUST READ.<br />Easily my favourite book this year, The Secret of Crickley Hall is the quintessential haunted house story. So often we pick up haunted house books thinking it's going to be full of ghosts and poltergeists and stormy nights and scary settings, only to spend 300 pages waiting for the ghosts to appear that never do.<br />This book is 600 pages of pure, unadulterated, haunted house goodness. There are good spirits, there are bad spirits, there is a big old manor, there is stormy weather, there is history and there is an abundance of supernatural in an abundance of forms.<br /><br />There is nothing more disappointing than picking up a book that you think is packed with ghosts and the ghosts never show up. This is certainly not that book.<br />A very easy five stars from me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13495792007903771300" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_356925284" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/356925284" />
    <a title="Melissa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3319099-melissa"><img alt="Melissa" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/356925284?book_show_action=true">Jun 27, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa" href="/user/show/3319099-melissa">Melissa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3319099-melissa?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3319099-melissa?shelf=could-not-finish">could-not-finish</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer356925284" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4558293838632736483">This goes on the 'could-not-finish' shelf. What a stinker. I was thoroughly impatient with the character descriptions and unnecessary explanations through dialogue, e.g., the mother explaining to the kindly old gardener why their youngest daughter is nicknamed "Callie"---I can almost picture the gardener nodding with polite disinterest. As an American, I was really irritated with the author feeling it necessary to include, during the mother's interior monologue, the information that her American</span>
  <span id="freeText4558293838632736483" style="display:none">This goes on the 'could-not-finish' shelf. What a stinker. I was thoroughly impatient with the character descriptions and unnecessary explanations through dialogue, e.g., the mother explaining to the kindly old gardener why their youngest daughter is nicknamed "Callie"---I can almost picture the gardener nodding with polite disinterest. As an American, I was really irritated with the author feeling it necessary to include, during the mother's interior monologue, the information that her American husband called the motorway the 'interstate' (even though he's lived in England for 16 years and is a mechanical engineer?). As if that weren't enough, she does this again later with "gorge" and "ravine". Hello Mr.Herbert? We have gorges in the States as well, no need to explain what one is. <br />Once the kindly old gardener showed up with his "West Country burr" thoughtfully re-produced for us in phonetic dialogue, I gave up. I'm not interested in being told through pointless exposition that the boot of a car is a trunk, or that cling film is plastic wrap. I already hate the mother and can see her turning into a major pain. Another peeve--it is also not necessary to show that a character is American by having him constantly say, "yeah" and "hey" and "gonna". Another inconsistency in the father's character;he is a MECHANICAL ENGINEER, i.e, he builds bridges and such, yet he doesn't know that a brook that is relatively mild during late summer might not get a bit wilder during the wetter months? Isn't knowing that stuff part of the job description of an mechanical engineer? Also, HAVING LIVED IN ENGLAND FOR SIXTEEN YEARS, doesn't he know what the weather is like? I can't be distracted with this kind of shoddy attention to detail alternating with boring attention detail (I refer you back to my comment re the youngest daughter's nickname). Especially when I'm reading a scary story. I'm the type, who while reading a recent Stephen King story was distracted by the fact that he had his character, a women in her late 30's remembering obscure 7UP jingles and Winston cigarette ads. I'm in my mid-40's and I never heard of the 7UP jingle(it likes you you like it). My husband is a few years older and he had never heard it either. I only know the Winston thing from having read an earlier King story. Maybe King was being meta and his character knew that stuff because she read his books? It didn't fly with me at all and that is a very minor detail (except for that he kept referring back to the 7UP thing). I just knew I was in for so much more in Herbert's book. I can't put myself through that. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4558293838632736483" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_591969851" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/591969851" />
    <a title="Rosie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13557596-rosie"><img alt="Rosie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1366472987p2/13557596.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/591969851?book_show_action=true">Apr 16, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rosie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rosie" href="/user/show/13557596-rosie">Rosie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780330411684" href="/book/show/397864.The_Secret_of_Crickley_Hall">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer591969851" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6170511010550392665"><b>Mind the spoilers!</b><br/><br/><b>Hmmm.</b> I think my overall impression of this book is that it was an interesting and compelling read, but just <i>too</i> long and repetitive, and at some points completely nonsensical.<br/><br/>I love a good ghost story and this one started off very well, with the Caleigh family heading to the very creepy Crickley Hall in Devon to get away from painful memories of their missing son on the first anniversary of his disappearance. It's the classic horror set up: main characters move to an unfamilia</span>
  <span id="freeText6170511010550392665" style="display:none"><b>Mind the spoilers!</b><br /><br /><b>Hmmm.</b> I think my overall impression of this book is that it was an interesting and compelling read, but just <i>too</i> long and repetitive, and at some points completely nonsensical.<br /><br />I love a good ghost story and this one started off very well, with the Caleigh family heading to the very creepy Crickley Hall in Devon to get away from painful memories of their missing son on the first anniversary of his disappearance. It's the classic horror set up: main characters move to an unfamiliar place; locals are a bit weird and unfriendly; old gardener/caretaker who may-or-may-not be creepy; moving into a house which is haunted by its tragic past; and last but not least, a good old-fashioned couple of villains. So the premise was right up my street...<br /><br /><br />...but then things got...<b>weird.</b><br /><br /><br />I understand that fiction demands the suspension of reality, particularly in a ghost story, but elements of the novel were so odd that it was sometimes difficult to know what to make of it. <br /><br />For instance, each member of the Caleigh family experiences ghostly goings-on in the house right from the first night, yet whenever one of them reports what they've seen the others refuse to believe them? Eve sees the shadowy dancing forms of the 'drowned' orphans in the house and Gabe follows a white shadow down into the cellar and squares up to something he can't see...but when Loren reports that a 'man' came to her bedroom and whipped her legs Gabe and Eve accuse her of dreaming, and take her to the doctor! <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[This despite the fact that the description she gives fits the profile of Augustus Cribben perfectly...and they have already found the cane which Loren describes stashed away in the noisy cupboard <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Their dog runs away, the cellar door opens itself every time they close it, constant puddles of water appear from nowhere, the lights go on and off, the rooms suddenly become freezing cold, and Eve is attacked by a malevolent figure in her sleep...but they don't leave the house, or even go out of their way to find out what's going on.<br /><br />Then there's Eve's 'psychic' connection with her missing son, Cam (his real name is Cameron, but they call him Cam...apparently that fact needs explaining to both the reader and other characters several times). How can Eve believe this, but have such a hard time realising she is clearly living in a majorly haunted house? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Anyway, the psychic connection turns out to be rubbish because sadly little Cam has been dead the whole time he's been missing...even though Eve 'could feel' he was alive and Lili nearly communicated with him....or so she says. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><br />I was also intrigued by the inexplicable fuss kicked up over the 'naked man' seen in Crickley Hall by Seraphina and her brother when they broke in. Why would their mother call the police on the Caleighs for that, and why would there be such a huge police turn out for it? As far as I know, it's not a crime to be naked in your own house! Even in front of two horrible little trespassers. Fair enough, it was a ghost...but do you call a police for a naked ghost sighting?<br /><br /><br />Then there's the constant repetition. How many times can similar things happen in one novel? I lost count of the times that somebody was frozen still by fear or smelt that soapy-rotting stink...not to mention how often Magda thinks about how smart and alert she is during one short chapter, as well as the frequent description towards the end of Maurice Stafford enjoying his brandy in the pub whilst flitting back and forth from his memories of the past.<br /><br />Also, for such a very, <i>very</i> long book, the characterisation was quite poor. Fair enough, I didn't want any of them to die, but they were very dull, with little personality. In fact, the only way James Herbert seems to try and build a little character is by doling out accents to the luckier ones, with Percy the gardener's speech often spelled out phonetically, and Gabe constantly using 'Americanisms' (not to mention being referred to over and over again as 'the American'). Eve wasn't vaguely interesting at all, and to be honest her reason for falling asleep at the park, allowing her son to go missing <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ or DROWN! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> (she's a fashion journalist and had been up late working on an article) did not inspire any sympathy in me at all really.<br /><br />All in all, I did enjoy this book while I was reading it (and reading it and reading it, because it never ends), but it could have done with being about 200 pages shorter, which would have been easily achievable by eliminating some of the repeated scenes.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6170511010550392665" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_934297027" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/934297027" />
    <a title="Chris" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1448151-chris"><img alt="Chris" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1566260753p2/1448151.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/934297027?book_show_action=true">May 11, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chris" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chris" href="/user/show/1448151-chris">Chris</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer934297027" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10799055820587215914">James Herbert, who passed away last year, has long been one of the most popular and influential horror writers since he first published The Rats in the late 70's. To many in the UK, he's their Stephen King, but Herbert is all his own, and for the uninitiated, you should read him, period.<br/><br/>The Secret of Crickley Hall is a classic haunted house tale, ranks right up there with the modern classics, such as The Haunting of Hill House, Hell House, The Shining, and Ghost Story. While the book is big and </span>
  <span id="freeText10799055820587215914" style="display:none">James Herbert, who passed away last year, has long been one of the most popular and influential horror writers since he first published The Rats in the late 70's. To many in the UK, he's their Stephen King, but Herbert is all his own, and for the uninitiated, you should read him, period.<br /><br />The Secret of Crickley Hall is a classic haunted house tale, ranks right up there with the modern classics, such as The Haunting of Hill House, Hell House, The Shining, and Ghost Story. While the book is big and dense in parts, it is all about layers and building the dread-laden suspense. <br /><br />The Caleigh family decides a break from the city, especially after the tragic disappearance of a family member nearly a year ago, is just what they need...and they settle for a few months in the old and rambling Crickley Hall, which has a tragic and dark history of its own. Then they begin to experience inexplicable events, mysterious noises in the dead of night, strange and frightening manifestations...and while they begin to question the reason behind the bizarre occurences, the truth is far more horrific than they could imagine.<br /><br />While perhaps not as graphic as some previous Herbert novels, this novel does not disappoint and one I thoroughly enjoyed.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10799055820587215914" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/220515221?book_show_action=true">Oct 08, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Deb" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Deb" href="/user/show/3687184-deb">Deb</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer220515221" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16412119134266994773">What's wrong with Crickley Hall? The cellar door won't stay shut. There are strange noises coming from the closet. The dog hates the place. Be very afraid, run away now - from this novel.<br/><br/>Oy, what a stinker. It has the bones of a good story - plotty enough that I had to severely edit the synopsis to be accepted by my book database - but the story is badly told and very badly edited. There is no real character development, although there are character back stories that take up valuable pages and a</span>
  <span id="freeText16412119134266994773" style="display:none">What's wrong with Crickley Hall? The cellar door won't stay shut. There are strange noises coming from the closet. The dog hates the place. Be very afraid, run away now - from this novel.<br /><br />Oy, what a stinker. It has the bones of a good story - plotty enough that I had to severely edit the synopsis to be accepted by my book database - but the story is badly told and very badly edited. There is no real character development, although there are character back stories that take up valuable pages and are left dangling. In an incredibly irritating dialog tic, the male lead, an American, speaks with "gonnas" and other colloquialisms and sounds like an idiot, not like an American. Rather than build the story organically, the author gives up pieces of information along the way through awkward exposition in the mouths of stock characters. Worst sin of all: not scary. The evil ghost is just laughable. Parts are base and lurid and left me feeling icky, but I was never once scared.﻿<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16412119134266994773" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2459977882" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2459977882" />
    <a title="Nick Imrie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5906293-nick-imrie"><img alt="Nick Imrie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591436280p2/5906293.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2459977882?book_show_action=true">Sep 29, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nick Imrie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nick Imrie" href="/user/show/5906293-nick-imrie">Nick Imrie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5906293-nick-imrie?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5906293-nick-imrie?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2459977882" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6654582632935437031">I read this 3 months ago and it's already slipping from my mind. What was the secret of Crickley Hall, again?<br/><br/>Oh yeah, I remember now, it's a completely generic haunted house. That's the secret. You know it's a haunted house because absolutely everyone comments on how gloomy and creepy it is the moment they step foot in it. And if that wasn't enough there's also a centenarian gardener who will drop not-very cryptic hints about the hauntings when he's not info-dumping the back story. Yes, the secr</span>
  <span id="freeText6654582632935437031" style="display:none">I read this 3 months ago and it's already slipping from my mind. What was the secret of Crickley Hall, again?<br /><br />Oh yeah, I remember now, it's a completely generic haunted house. That's the secret. You know it's a haunted house because absolutely everyone comments on how gloomy and creepy it is the moment they step foot in it. And if that wasn't enough there's also a centenarian gardener who will drop not-very cryptic hints about the hauntings when he's not info-dumping the back story. Yes, the secret of Crickley Hall is explained and repeated ad nauseum by multiple different characters and flash-backs, but what's never explained is why a grieving family with only two children would choose to live in an enormous, gloomy, isolated, obviously haunted mansion. Just think of the energy bills.<br /><br />It was just so disappointingly unscary. It had all the elements of a good haunting - strange puddles of water appearing, strange knockings, doors swinging open on their own. Yet none of these elements were properly deployed to produce fear. In a good horror there's some suspense: doors creaking open on their own are the first inexorable step to the confrontation with evil. If the doors are just swinging about willy-nilly then you've got yourself a DIY problem.<br /><br />But the real problem was that the characters were so wooden. I wasn't scared by the horror, and largely neither were they, apparently being too stupid to realise they were in a haunted house, even though the mother was a firm believer in the supernatural, and every one of them had an encounter with the ghosts. And indeed the book itself seemed rather confused about whether or not the ghosts were scary. Sometimes it was the manifestion of the poor children, not threatening but crying out for justice, and sometimes the manifestion of their terrible abuser who in life had only ever been a threat to helpless kids, and seemed equally impotent in death.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6654582632935437031" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText9508456217291185738" style="display:none">I'll admit to skimming through parts of this book. Mostly, the parts that repeated, and repeated...and repeated. My Lord, the ENDLESS repetition. First one person tells the story, then another, then we get a flashback memory of the story, then a summary and then yet another person tells the same story again. Sigh.<br />No mystery here, no scares or creepy scenes (though plenty were meant to be)- the most disturbing parts (aside from the poorly executed and, yes, repetitious, "Americanisms") were the descriptions of child murder, which were a bit too graphic for the story. <br />I finished this because it was a quick read. If I had to spend more than one sitting reading it, I would never have finished.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1579234889" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1579234889" />
    <a title="Benjamin Stahl" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16968146-benjamin-stahl"><img alt="Benjamin Stahl" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592923113p2/16968146.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1579234889?book_show_action=true">Mar 14, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Benjamin Stahl" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Benjamin Stahl" href="/user/show/16968146-benjamin-stahl">Benjamin Stahl</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Dumbshits</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16968146-benjamin-stahl?shelf=buddy-reads">buddy-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1579234889" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16441382723289570458"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459596221i/18631751._SX540_.jpg' width='“400"' height='250' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>This book seriously has me stuck. I’m totally split about whether to rate it two or three stars. I could just get a life and not care about it either way, but this is me we’re talking about. So here goes an in-depth discussion with myself which I really haven't the time to indulge in. <br/>Shit. I <i>hated</i> this book. Aside from the suicide letter I wrote my parents some months ago, it was probably the most disappointing thing I've read in a long time. (The former being disappointing because obviously I</span>
  <span id="freeText16441382723289570458" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459596221i/18631751._SX540_.jpg" width='“400"' height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>This book seriously has me stuck. I’m totally split about whether to rate it two or three stars. I could just get a life and not care about it either way, but this is me we’re talking about. So here goes an in-depth discussion with myself which I really haven't the time to indulge in. <br>Shit. I <i>hated</i> this book. Aside from the suicide letter I wrote my parents some months ago, it was probably the most disappointing thing I've read in a long time. (The former being disappointing because obviously I didn't go through with it). <br><br>At 600 pages, it felt basically like an overlong dummy's guide to writing ghost stories. By that I mean it was, in all technical sense, a competent effort. James Herbert is a lot of things, but he ain't no sloppy writer. He knows what words to use when, and, like, he doesn’t write like a fucking idiot. No, what I mean by “dummy's guide” is that <i>Crickley Hall</i> is little more than an overstuffed demonstration of formulaic cliches which have formed the basis of this genre for over a century. Think of any trope that appears in any haunted house film you’ve seen, any book you’ve read, and the chances are its somewhere in this book. And what pissed me off most if that it isn’t even done that <i>well</i> here!! <br><br>As my fellow buddy-reader Aileene would attest to, fucking the ghosts were not <i>scary</i>. In my opinion, the scariest thing in this book was the back flap, where I was suddenly exposed to a picture of the author. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459596124i/18631725._SX540_.jpg" width='“400"' height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I'll admit I was not expecting <i>that</i>. The delivery of this moment - (the grotesque imagery; the ominous implication in the pursing of his lips) - is downright genius. It shall keep me up for weeks. But as for the <i>rest</i> of the story? Well, <u>unforutely</u>, I would say “forget it”. <br>What scares <i>me</i> is the auto-correct on my Evernote. It frightens me because I recently submitted an essay for university, and I wrote the damned thing on this. Guess the "mystery mark" at least has the mystery element, which I always enjoy. (<i>Did I get 30% or was it even worse? I’ll never know, and I’ll spend the rest of the year speculating with my Goodreads friends</i>).<br><br>All jokes aside though, I am a fan of Herbert’s work. Though I generally consider him more of a "guilty pleasure”. The first book I read of his was <i>The Ghosts Of Sleath</i>. And guess what? That book <i>terrified</i> me. After <i>Dracula</i>, <i>It</i> and <i>The Exorcist</i>, it's probably one of the creepiest books I’ve read. This was followed by his most famous novel, <i>Haunted</i>, which was also the predecessor to <i>Sleath</i>. Sad to say, I was not a big fan of that book. I much prefer the film starring Aidan Quinn and an early Kate Beckinsale performance I had a major crush on as a kid.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459596124i/18631726.jpg" width='“400"' height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Aside from <i>Fluke</i>, which is my favourite of Herbert’s books so far, the rest were just mediocre trudges between average and occasionally disturbing. I was not overly impressed with <i>The Rats</i>, <i>The Spear</i>, <i>The Fog</i>, or the slightly more decent <i>The Survivor</i>. I grew tired of Herbert’s repetitious style very quickly, and while I was initially intrigued in reading <i>Crickley Hall</i> for the fact that it came much later in his sadly-ended career, I found myself becoming increasingly discouraged ... soon disappointed ... and eventually <i>infuriated</i> with his apparent lack of original thinking. <br>The “Haunted House”, while one of my favourites, is admittedly a stale subject in today’s film and literature. It can still be invigorated - (as was proved by King’s <i>Bag Of Bones</i> and Wan's film <i>Insidious</i>, to name just a few) - but artists really need to justify themselves when returning to this concept. Similar to the “Zombie Apocalypse”, it’s become so commonplace that it instantly fails to captivate unless it brings something new to the table. And while I will now go on to explain how this book finally <i>did</i> start paying its dues, I still have no hesitation in saying that with <i>Crickley Hall</i>, James Herbert does nothing new nor interesting with the material <i>whatsoever</i>. <br><br>That is why I hated this book. It was such a terrible case of <b>WASTED POTENTIAL</b>. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459596124i/18631727.jpg" width='“400"' height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Oh my God, is that supposed to be <i>Augustus Cribben</i>? But he doesn’t look scary <i>at all</i>!!</b> <br><br>This is where my review changes. Because at about 400 pages in, something very annoying happened. You ever get those times when you read a book halfway through, and you pretty much hate it? It angers you so much, in fact, that you start planning your hilarious rant as you force yourself on through the pages? And then, towards the end, feeling like you have a valid criticism to make, the author pulls a fast one and the story you hated finally starts falling into place?<br>Something very much the same happened to me with Kathryn Stockett's <i>The Help</i>. I thought that was terrible for the first 100-200 pages. But then towards the end I found myself grateful I was reading it in private. If I had recited the damned book in class I would have blubbered like a little girl. (Exageration, there ... but yes, I was won over by that book in the end). And <i>Crickley Hall</i> does the same bloody thing!!<br><br>After 400 pages of <i>bullshit</i>. Obvious paranormal activity, and there's Mr Fucking Cynic writing it off as <i>reflections in the window frame</i>. "Hey, Gabe, you dickhead. Look at that ghost walking across the upstairs landing!! Sweet mercy of <i>Christ</i>, my heart is on the <i>brink</i>!!”<br>“Aww, s’no ghost, Slim,” says Mr Colloquialism. Fucking contradicting me. “That gruesome human figure you see walking across the landing, grabbing my daughter by the hair and slamming her face against the balustrade, is just a phenomena I like to call <i>dust motes</i>”.<br><br>“Gabe, <i>lookout</i>!! There's a spectral demon about to wallop you with its punishment stick!! - <i>Ohh</i>, there he goes!! Gee, are you okay, man?"<br>“Aww, s’not anything to get alarmed about,” says Mr Fucking Downtoearth. “It’s just these cracks in the floor. They cause air currents to rise from the cellar and mingle with the chandelier’s reflection in the recently-varnished oak walls”.<br>“Gabe,” I mutter, shaking my head. “Come here. I’m going to hit you”. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459596124i/18631728._SX540_.jpg" width='“400"' height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><b>Loren and Cally. Just as bored as Aileene and I were.</b><br><br>But as I was saying, this book did come around in the end. That’s not to say that it became amazing. But things finally got a little more intense. Things in the house started happening that were not just dismissed as being mice in the roof. I have to say that I was mostly disappointed with the lack of gratuitous sex and violence in this book. Generally, Herbert’s books are full of that shit, and there's me acting like an asshole and complaining about it. <br>But then he takes that stuff out and I’m fucking upset about it <i>not</i> being there. I don’t know what’s wrong with me. I’m seeing a psychiatrist and staying off Facebook and pretending that the world doesn’t exist. The new Weezer album came out yesterday and that’s provided me with some needed escapism. <br><br>There was no sex in this book, so shit, there goes that. (Oh, I just remembered, there was <i>some</i> sex ... between a middle-aged woman and a little boy). And yeah, the violence was surprisingly toned down as well. Until the end, that is. Near the end, things get pretty fucked, and though I felt like a horrible person, I was so happily disturbed when Herbert starting adding his trademark sprinkle of sadism to the mix. <br><br><b>Circumcisions … you gotta love 'em.</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1396297083i/9112899.jpg" width='“400"' height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>This book was really pretty bad for the first half. It gave me the shits, and I also had to take the blame for choosing this book for my first buddy read with Aileene. Have you ever taken a girl to the movies, except the film turns out shit, and at one point you lean closer and whisper, “Hey, we don’t have to watch this if you don’t want. Let’s just get some ice-cream instead”. And then she nudges you away, shifts angrily aside, and says, “I don’t think so, mate. You made me pay for this shit, now we're gonna watch it. <i>Asshole</i>”. <br><br>I'm angry with Herbert for letting me down, and if he wasn’t dead I would go to him and express my dissatisfaction. "No, I’m not asking for a refund. I just want to look you in the eye, and tell you I was unhappy with your product. I want those words to haunt your dreams tonight”. Customers are always saying shit like that to me at work. <br><br>So in closing, I guess I wanted and could have said more. But let’s not be superfluous. I’ve already managed to slip in yet another suicide reference, as well as a miniature review for <i>The Help</i>. I really don’t know what I’m doing. I threw a 5kg weight into the damn on my property this afternoon. I made the affirmation that the demon in my brain was reconfigured into that object, and then I threw it into the dam. I closed my eyes and deeply inhaled. I entered the realm of normality again. Except writing this review is already bringing that demon back. I’m going to log off and punch myself in the face now. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16441382723289570458" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3622367421" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3622367421" />
    <a title="Phil" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/76396700-phil"><img alt="Phil" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1516033071p2/76396700.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3622367421?book_show_action=true">Nov 01, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Phil" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Phil" href="/user/show/76396700-phil">Phil</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/76396700-phil?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3622367421" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14971553060593910545">Pretty tame outing for Herbert to be sure. Basically, this is something of a 'classic' haunted house story, albeit it reads almost like a mystery. The Caleigh family moves into Crickley Hall, an old manor house near a small harbor town. Gabe (the father) has some local work to do (he is an engineer) and hopes the temporary move will help him and especially his wife, for it is almost a year since their son Cam has gone missing. Eve, the wife, fell asleep at a park in London, and when she awoke Ca</span>
  <span id="freeText14971553060593910545" style="display:none">Pretty tame outing for Herbert to be sure. Basically, this is something of a 'classic' haunted house story, albeit it reads almost like a mystery. The Caleigh family moves into Crickley Hall, an old manor house near a small harbor town. Gabe (the father) has some local work to do (he is an engineer) and hopes the temporary move will help him and especially his wife, for it is almost a year since their son Cam has gone missing. Eve, the wife, fell asleep at a park in London, and when she awoke Cam was gone without a trace. Still blaming herself, she has been in mourning ever since. Their two remaining children-- girls age 12 and 5-- move with them to Crickley Hall-- a stark, forbidding house to be sure. It turns out no one stays in Crickley Hall long, as they are informed by the old gardener who kinda comes with the place. <br /><br />Obviously, something terrible happened at Crickley Hall back in 1943. It seems the house, being vacant at the time, was hastily turned into a school for some orphans from London seeking to escape the blitz. In 1943 there was a terrible flood which killed dozens of people and the orphans as well, at least that is the story that is commonly told. As the story unfolds, however, we learn more about the orphans and their two guardians, one of which died the night of the flood and the other was found the next day at a train station, but she would not speak ever again and is now in a resting home. So, what happened at Crickley Hall, what is the secret? Well, it takes Herbert about 600 pages for that to come out...<br /><br />This was definitely a slow burn type of novel, and while punctuated with some trills, is pretty slow going. A good editor probably could have lopped off a few hundred pages or so with good effect as Herbert repeats several things over and over. He did a good job with character development (perhaps too good) and we really feel we know the Caleighs by the end. The entire story takes place in just one week. I know this was toward the end of his writing career, but it still lacks the punch of his earlier work. 3 spooky stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14971553060593910545" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_373698226" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/373698226" />
    <a title="Chris Jay" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11129697-chris-jay"><img alt="Chris Jay" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/373698226?book_show_action=true">Jul 21, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chris Jay" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chris Jay" href="/user/show/11129697-chris-jay">Chris Jay</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780330411684" href="/book/show/397864.The_Secret_of_Crickley_Hall">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer373698226" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3664786626641936669">Well, what can I say, I bought this book on the 20th, and have just finished it today, 3 days later, despite the books 633 pages.<br/><br/>Where do I start? Just please, if you enjoy an amazing plot, twists that left me literally gasping, (And I'm not one to over react) biting my nails, and on the verge of tears at points, then pick up The Secret of Crickely Hall.<br/><br/>Other reviews deterred me from reading this, and I picked it up with half heartedness, and the intention of dropping it after the first 80 pages</span>
  <span id="freeText3664786626641936669" style="display:none">Well, what can I say, I bought this book on the 20th, and have just finished it today, 3 days later, despite the books 633 pages.<br /><br />Where do I start? Just please, if you enjoy an amazing plot, twists that left me literally gasping, (And I'm not one to over react) biting my nails, and on the verge of tears at points, then pick up The Secret of Crickely Hall.<br /><br />Other reviews deterred me from reading this, and I picked it up with half heartedness, and the intention of dropping it after the first 80 pages. (Another reviewer had said, i was bored rigid by the first 80 pages.) Well after my first sitting, I had read the first 200 odd pages, and the only reason I stopped was it was approaching 2 am!<br /><br />The characters are great and more to the point, believable. Throughout the book I was left there thinking, I DO THAT, notably the part where Eve mimics the tea drinking to Percy when offering him a cup.<br /><br />The twists, and ending especially, are nail biting and shocking. I was left aghast and couldn't turn the pages fast enough to find out what was happening next! Contrary to other reviews on here, this book is definitely a well thought and planned piece, and it is reflected in the nerve shredding climatic ending, which Herbert portrays masterfully through his glorious use of language.<br /><br />But the plot is what makes this book. I have read many horror novels, all of which run out of things to say, and end up repeating themselves, (notably Cell by S. King), whereas this book doesn't. We find things out in perfect timing, and as the story unfolds the book just gets better and better and better. The use of different monologues from the different characters, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[notably in chapter 71 : caught <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> gives good perspectives of what happened in Crickely Hall all them years ago without it turning into a long wall of text being blurted from one character. It is a brilliant combination of imagery <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[from Lili <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, and monologue <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[from Maurice <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, which paints a detailed vivid picture in the readers mind. <br /><br />Please, if you enjoy reading horror books, ignore the other reviews from people who have given up on it before it really picks up. Yes the storyline is EXTREMELY DARK, and does involve children, BUT if you can look past that, you will be reading the best novel I have ever had the pleasure to read.<br /><br /><u>
  <b>DEFINITELY NOT ONE TO MISS</b>
</u><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3664786626641936669" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9143110638410369220">Horror seems to be James Herbert's talent, from his creepy little novel <i>The Rats</i> to this one, which, instead of featuring an apocalypse-like scenario with animals, instead focuses on a more eerie and sinister plot. In <i>The Secret of Crickley Hall</i>, the ghosts of wrongfully-treated children are the center of the plot.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_423625827" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/423625827" />
    <a title="Alexander Smith" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8527846-alexander-smith"><img alt="Alexander Smith" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1554128919p2/8527846.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/423625827?book_show_action=true">Sep 28, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alexander Smith" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alexander Smith" href="/user/show/8527846-alexander-smith">Alexander Smith</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer423625827" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6306917792920635921">I think the best-kept secret of Crickley Hall is the fact that absolutely nothing exciting happens there… Which is a shame, because I am a huge James Herbert fan, and have just finished reading Others (review to come), which was absolutely brilliant. But this book felt like a shade of his other ghost stories, something that looks at first glance like it should be perfectly terrifying, but which soon grows stale and familiar and dull. It’s like that moment when you wake up at night and see the sp</span>
  <span id="freeText6306917792920635921" style="display:none">I think the best-kept secret of Crickley Hall is the fact that absolutely nothing exciting happens there… Which is a shame, because I am a huge James Herbert fan, and have just finished reading Others (review to come), which was absolutely brilliant. But this book felt like a shade of his other ghost stories, something that looks at first glance like it should be perfectly terrifying, but which soon grows stale and familiar and dull. It’s like that moment when you wake up at night and see the spectre in your room, and have that soul-jolting mix of fear and excitement, only to realise that the shape you see is the dressing gown on the back of the door. This book is a dressing gown.<br /><br />So what’s wrong with it…? Ostensibly it’s got great foundations for a ghost story: a family suffering from the loss of a son move to a new town to make a fresh start. And where better to forget all about death? A gloomy mansion in a middle-of-nowhere place called Devil’s Cleave. And the book starts well, with some chilling moments – a creepy disused well in the cellar and a door that won’t stay closed, eerie noises, old toys discarded in the attic, and a backstory about something awful that happened in the house a long time ago…<br /><br />Hang on, isn’t all this sounding a little familiar? Yup. And from Herbert too. He’s essentially ripped himself off to create a ghost story that we’ve all heard before. There are elements of his other, and much better, novels here: Ghosts of Sleath and Haunted to name just two. These recycled horror tropes are so familiar that they just aren’t scary any more. It ends up being utterly clichéd, completely predictable. I held out because I thought there would be an amazing twist at the end, something to make the journey worthwhile, but the climax (well, the conclusion, it was anything but climactic) is the same old tired fare. You can see it coming from so far away that I actually felt angry when we got there.<br /><br />The book’s worst crime, though, is the massive amount of exposition that we’re force-fed throughout. So much of the story is just that – a story – told by one of the characters. And not particularly well told at that. At one point, the guy reciting this soulless account even says, “Ah, I can tell I’m boring you.” You don’t say! It’s almost as if Herbert himself is confessing, "sorry guys, I know this sucks, I'll do better next time, promise!" It’s chapter after chapter of wittering monologue that pulls us away from what little action the book has and makes us sit twiddling our thumbs while the tedious back story grinds endlessly on. Reading this was a little bit like listening to an elderly relative drunk on sherry trying to recount a book he read half a century ago. It was excruciatingly bad.<br /><br />Okay, I should add a disclaimer before finishing this review. I was reading this book on my phone, on a ten-hour train journey back from Scotland, so I was probably in a foul mood anyway. But I read countless books on my phone on long journeys, and none have infuriated me as much as this one. Crickley Hall hasn’t put me off James Herbert. He’s one of the finest horror writers on the planet, and some of his books are sheer genius. This, sadly, is not one of them. Read something else by him, because The Secret of Crickley Hall should be left a shameful secret that as few people as possible come to discover. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6306917792920635921" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText1410608697708925511" style="display:none">This novel ticks all the traditional ghost story boxes - a creepy old house in the middle of nowhere, cut off from the mainland by a river, doors that won't stay closed, inexplicable pools of water in the the hall, mysterious bangs in the middle of the night, and a decades old mystery which is the cause of the hauntings. <br />It should work, but I'm afraid I found this book dreadfully verbose. Herbert isn't content to tell you something once. The same information is provided over and over again which made me, the reader, feel very patronized. I don't need phonetic spellings of dialogue spoken in a Devonshire accent. This book is in serious need of a good editor. If it was halved, it would be so much more effective. <br />As others have pointed out, the reason for the hauntings at Crickley Hall is pretty hard to stomach, and I found some of the detail unnecessarily sadistic. <br />Hard to recommend I'm afraid. </span>

<div id="review_2420456206" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2420456206" />
    <a title="Andrew “The Weirdling” Glos" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11108582-andrew-the-weirdling-glos"><img alt="Andrew “The Weirdling” Glos" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1524324282p2/11108582.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2420456206?book_show_action=true">Jun 14, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andrew “The Weirdling” Glos" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andrew “The Weirdling” Glos" href="/user/show/11108582-andrew-the-weirdling-glos">Andrew “The Weirdling” Glos</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11108582-andrew-the-weirdling-glos?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11108582-andrew-the-weirdling-glos?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2420456206" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8657384478052668589">The thing about James Herbert books is that they aren’t original, groundbreaking, or genre bending in any way. If you imagine a stereotypical scary story, Herbert will put in every scene you expect in pretty much the way you expect it. Red Panda says it’s as if he starts his stories with a check list and goes down the boxes one at a time and ticks them all off. That’s accurate. He’s a formula writer. That may sounds bad. Usually it is. But not with Herbert. The fact of the matter is he’s a maste</span>
  <span id="freeText8657384478052668589" style="display:none">The thing about James Herbert books is that they aren’t original, groundbreaking, or genre bending in any way. If you imagine a stereotypical scary story, Herbert will put in every scene you expect in pretty much the way you expect it. Red Panda says it’s as if he starts his stories with a check list and goes down the boxes one at a time and ticks them all off. That’s accurate. He’s a formula writer. That may sounds bad. Usually it is. But not with Herbert. The fact of the matter is he’s a master of formulas. He reminds you of why the formula exists in the first place and why they keep being used and reused. He shows you - after a long spell of reading formula scary stories written by far lesser talents - just how good the formula can be. If you are like me, you will enjoy seeing it done so masterfully that you never once get irritated that you see it all coming long before it arrives. <br /><br />So, in a way, it’s hard to give him a five star review for any of his books. (I don’t think I have yet.) But it’s also hard to give him less than a four. <br /><br />The Secret of Crickley Hall is classic Herbert. A family with emotionally crippling back story decides to “get away from it all for a while”. They rent a cost effective house that turns out to have a tragic backstory of its own. The house has strange occurrences that get stranger. Then - oh my gosh - the haunted looking house turns out to be haunted house! Who knew?! Oh wait, half the town actually knew but they never talk about it. They just gave knowing looks to one another every time the family was in town and make obscure references in front of them. No worries, though, because there’s an old crust caretaker who also knows and tells them in confidence. What a nice bloke to let them in on the secret. Of course, he knows more than he says and is more involved then he lets on. But that will all come out later. Ultimately, crisis crescendos when the mom and kids are trapped alone in the house and the dad is struggling to get back, the ghosts get uppity, and someone turns out to not be who we thought. <br /><br />Like I said- if you’ve read 5+ haunted house tales or seen movies, then you could write this book yourself. You won’t be shocked by any plot twists. That said, you will enjoy the writing, the characters, the use of old standbys doing what archetypal pattern characters are supposed to do. <br /><br />It is a very ably executed book, as all Herbert’s books have been so far. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8657384478052668589" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2811383978" class="readable"
